Little Western Paradise

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Fourteen: A Different Enlightenment: A Westerner Discusses Construction; A Poor Scholar Plants Seeds of Love

But with Beihai walking around here, Zhiqian's interest was piqued, anticipating some action to follow. He continued to hold the door, peeking outside. Sure enough, after a short while, Beihai turned around and came back to the doorway. He stood with his hands behind his back, one foot extended at an angle, his eyes looking towards Aunt Hu's house. For about five minutes, he didn't move his feet. Then, he raised his head to look at the evening glow in the sky, and then turned his head to look around at the houses and gates in the alley, moving his feet west for about twenty steps. When he walked, his steps were very slow. But when he turned around, he quickly returned to the original spot. Once there, he did nothing but look up, then turn his head to look at both ends of the alley. He didn't pay much attention to Aunt Hu's house across the street, only glancing at it occasionally. It was at this moment that Zhu Yueying flashed by in the courtyard across the street, immediately entering the house, but she came out again in less than a minute. Looking at her, she seemed to have something very heavy on her mind. She leaned against the wall, walking with her head down. When she reached her gate, she first put a finger in her mouth. At that time, her eyes were naturally looking down. There was a young scholar standing across the street, but she didn't seem to see him. Beihai's attitude was exactly the same, very casual, not paying attention to the girl coming out across the street. Yueying reached the gate and finally took her finger out of her mouth. Then, she held onto the doorframe with both hands, looked up at the sky, and said to herself: "Who says it looks like it's going to rain? The weather is very nice." (241)

The Fragrant Memoirs of the Imperial Incense

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of the Qing Dynasty, translated by Qin Shouou

At that time, it was Li Lianying's turn to serve again. He first took out a specially made horn and blew it three or four times. Thus, the two small boats, equipped with stoves and already prepared with wine and dishes for the Empress Dowager, quickly rowed closer, one on the left and one on the right, docking on either side of the imperial boat. Then, the people on the imperial boat brought out two specially prepared gangplanks and placed them between the large boat and the small boats. The eunuchs then busily walked back and forth on the gangplanks, preparing to start bringing out the Empress Dowager's lunch.

Today, perhaps because they were afraid of things rolling, breaking, or sinking into the lake on the boat, all the dishes were made of gold or silver. Only the chopsticks used by the Empress Dowager were still the same jade chopsticks she used every day, not changed. As for the eunuchs carrying the dishes, because the space on the boat was narrow, it was inconvenient to run around, so they had to imitate the method used on the train last time, lining up in two very organized rows, one on the left and one on the right, all the way from the gangplanks to the two small boats on either side. All the dishes were then passed up one by one. However, the eunuchs all temporarily covered their hands with a clean white cloth to prevent their fingers from directly touching the Empress Dowager's food. The number of dishes was still a hundred as usual, not reduced by even a bit. But because the tables on the boat were much smaller after all, and there really wasn't enough space, they had to put a few cold dishes and desserts on the table first, and let the remaining ones be held by the eunuchs for the time being. Fortunately, each bowl and plate was covered with a lid, so that the food inside could be kept at its original temperature. The Empress Dowager chewed on the few dishes that were served first while talking to me. I also tried my best to entertain her, hoping to keep her happy throughout. (341)

A History of Lamps

— (Xian Fa)

In ancient times, light was obtained by bundling grass or weaving bamboo into torches, and there was nothing called a lamp. Later, when oil was discovered, there were oil lamps and candles. After kerosene was discovered, there were kerosene lamps. After gas was discovered, there were gas lamps. Today, everyone can use electric lamps.

Lamps originated six hundred years before the Common Era. Shells, bones, and fruit shells were used as lamps, burning vegetable oil or animal fat. From two hundred years before the Common Era to three hundred years after, clay lamps were used, commonly known as early clay lamps. From three hundred to one thousand years, colored ceramic lamps were used, all burning vegetable oil. From one thousand to one thousand six hundred years, copper lamps were used, burning olive oil. From one thousand six hundred to one thousand eight hundred years, Berta lamps were used, burning fat oil. From one thousand eight hundred to one thousand eight hundred and fifty years, candles began to be used. From one thousand eight hundred and fifty to one thousand eight hundred and seventy years, Confin lamps were used. In one thousand eight hundred and seventy years, kerosene lamps were used again. In one thousand eight hundred and ninety years, carbon lamps were used. In one thousand nine hundred and ten years, Marilda lamps were used. In one thousand nine hundred and twenty years, white Marilda lamps were used. In one thousand nine hundred and twenty-seven years, internal milky electric lamps were used.

In summary, it can be divided into three major periods. Before six hundred years before the Common Era, it can be called the torch period. Afterwards, it was the oil lamp period. After one thousand eight hundred and ninety years, it can be called the electric lamp period. This is a rough outline of the world's lamp history.

Local Customs Sketches

Talking About the Buddhist Scriptures Stored in Longhua Temple

— Shanghai Communication Society

Yesterday, all the Shanghai newspapers carried a piece of news about Longhua Temple organizing the Ming Dynasty Wanli Emperor's bestowed Tripitaka. Because Longhua Temple is in Shanghai, we, who are studying Shanghai's position, feel that we can no longer remain silent upon seeing that "barbarian head" style of news.

If you flip through the county chronicles of the Qing Dynasty's Kangxi, Qianlong, Jiaqing, and Tongzhi reigns, there are the same records about Longhua Temple being granted a Tripitaka during the Ming Dynasty's Wanli reign. They roughly say: At that time, the emperor issued an edict granting Buddhist scriptures to famous mountains. The abbot of Longhua Temple, the monk Da Guo, petitioned for it to be granted, and received the emperor's permission. He specially sent a eunuch to the temple to bestow the Tripitaka in seven hundred and eighteen cases, and also bestowed a golden ring and purple robes to Da Guo for protecting the scriptures. However, if you flip through the Continued Chronicle of Shanghai County, it also says that in the thirteenth year of the Tongzhi reign of the Qing Dynasty (1874), a Tripitaka was requested, which the so-called Longhua Temple's reviving founder, the monk Guan Zhu, received from the ministry. In Zi Tao's "Miscellaneous Records of Ying Yuan," it was also said: "...In the summer of Jiaxu, the abbot Guan Zhu received the Tripitaka from the ministry, prepared ceremonial guards to welcome it, with about a hundred monks escorting it. After the war, the Buddhist teachings flourished day by day, and this is its sign." From this, we can know that Longhua Temple has had two Tripitakas one after another. Then the fact must be turned to the topic above, is the Tripitaka that Longhua Temple is organizing the one bestowed during the Ming Dynasty's Wanli reign? Or the one bestowed during the Qing Dynasty's Tongzhi reign? According to the abbot Xing Kong's determination, it is undoubtedly the one bestowed during the Ming Dynasty. And the Dharma Master Mantuo, who was invited by Xing Kong and who had organized the Tripitaka in Huayan Temple in Chongqing, also did not deny it. The news was published that way, and the readers believed it that way. However, according to the research results of our Shanghai Communication Society, the Tripitaka currently in Longhua Temple is definitely not the Ming Dynasty Wanli edition, but the "Long Tripitaka edition" bestowed during the Qing Dynasty's Tongzhi reign. Now we can write down some of the research results:

According to the Dharma Master Mantuo's preliminary organization of the Tripitaka, he said that the entire Tripitaka has thirteen volumes per case, excluding the table of contents, with a total of seven hundred and thirty cases. Upon inspection, there are three hundred and fifty-nine complete cases, three hundred and nineteen incomplete cases, and fifty-three completely lost cases. In terms of the number of cases, if it is the Ming Dynasty Wanli edition, then according to the county chronicle's record, it should be seven hundred and eighteen cases, but now there are seven hundred and thirty cases excluding the table of contents, which shows that it is definitely not the Ming Dynasty Wanli edition but the Long Tripitaka edition, because the total number of the Long Tripitaka edition is seven hundred and thirty-five cases. This is one.

Furthermore, regarding the format. The Ming Dynasty Wanli edition of the Tripitaka was initiated by the two Chan masters Mi Zang and Huan Yu in the seventeenth year of the Shenzong Wanli reign (1589). At that time, the great masters Ganshan Zibo, as well as Yuan Liaofan, Feng Mengzhen, and others vigorously supported it, and the printing was done at Jing Mountain Lengyan Temple. It took decades to complete the printing. The style at that time was a square-bound style. As for the Long Tripitaka edition, it was printed from the thirteenth year of the Qing Dynasty's Shizong Yongzheng reign (1735) to the third year of the Gaozong Qianlong reign (1738), using the "Northern Tripitaka edition" as a draft. The format is Sanskrit-style, with five lines per page, the same as the Shu edition format. The Shanghai Communication Society reporter has also seen the Tripitaka in Longhua Temple now. It is indeed Sanskrit-style and only has five lines per page, so it is determined that it is not the one bestowed during the Ming Dynasty Wanli reign, but the one bestowed during the Qing Dynasty Tongzhi reign. This is two.

Furthermore, regarding the history of Longhua Temple itself, according to the records of the Tongzhi County Chronicle and the Miscellaneous Records of Ying Yuan, Longhua Temple was destroyed when the Taiping army attacked Shanghai in the tenth year of the Xianfeng reign (1860). Regarding the Tripitaka bestowed during the Ming Dynasty, although it does not state that it was also destroyed, it also does not say that it was not destroyed. So, according to our current guess, unless the abbot of Longhua Temple received the news in advance and moved the Tripitaka away; otherwise, it would be that the monks valued the Buddhist scriptures so much that they were willing to sacrifice their lives and return to the Western Paradise with the Buddhist scriptures. In the meantime, they desperately carried the Tripitaka to escape, but even if they carried it, would it be possible to carry that many volumes? Therefore, we can know that the Tripitaka bestowed during the Ming Dynasty Wanli reign was mostly burned at that time; and the one now is the one bestowed during the Qing Dynasty Tongzhi reign.

Finally, the Shanghai Communication Society greatly admires Abbot Xing Kong's actions in organizing the Tripitaka; but we hope that the history will not be mistaken, turning into what Shanghai people call "selling barbarian heads"!

(4) Send letters to each agency to check the service personnel and fill out a form to participate in sports programs. Education News

Jiangxi, Sichuan, and Henan Provinces; Compulsory Education Funding Confirmed

(Nanjing, 16th) The Ministry of Education received follow-up telegrams from Jiangxi, Sichuan, Henan and other provinces on the 16th regarding the matter of various provinces and cities planning local compulsory education funds. Jiangxi's implementation of compulsory education is to universally set up school security measures. In the next year, it is determined to add 6,000 school security measures, which require funding of 1,578,000 yuan. Local and provincial treasuries can jointly raise 820,000 yuan. The counties in Sichuan plan to set up a total of 2,749 schools, which require a total of 1,314,500 yuan. The province will raise 660,000 yuan itself. Henan plans to set up 4,400 short-term primary schools in a ten-year plan, and the funding has also been arranged.

Guizhou Province Promotes Compulsory Education Plan

(Central News Agency, Guiyang, 14th) The Department of Education received an order from the Ministry of Education on the 13th, instructing it to draft measures for promoting compulsory education, consult with the chairman of the province, and report to the Ministry by the 14th of this month, as a standard for the central government to allocate compulsory education funds. After receiving the order, the Department of Education immediately planned to set up short-term primary schools in the province and raise funds. According to the plan, a total of 850 short-term schools will be set up throughout the province, requiring a total of 212,500 yuan. The plan has been submitted to the provincial government for review.

Ministry of Education Promulgates and Implements; Key Points of Specific Measures for Compulsory Education

The Ministry of Education plans to promote compulsory education starting in the 24th year of the Republic of China. In addition to the Outline of Measures for Implementing Compulsory Education, which has been promulgated by the Executive Yuan and issued to the competent authorities of various provinces and cities, requiring them to properly draft implementation plans and submit them for record, the Ministry also announced the detailed rules for the implementation of the outline on the 15th of this month. These detailed rules are a concrete plan for the promotion of compulsory education and are of utmost importance. Yesterday, this newspaper briefly described it. Now, the main points are recorded below.

1. Short-term primary schools shall explicitly stipulate the exemption of tuition fees and enrollment fees. Those located in rural areas may have holidays during the busy farming season to facilitate farming operations.

2. Enact compulsory enrollment laws. In areas where the local primary schools are sufficient to accommodate local school-age children, all healthy school-age children should be supervised to enroll. If they do not enroll, their parents or guardians should be persuaded to enroll them. Those who do not heed the persuasion may have their names posted publicly. If they still do not comply, they may be fined from one to five yuan. However, those who have illnesses or other reasons may request exemption from school with a certificate. The fines will still be used for compulsory education.

3. Preparations. Each locality should divide school districts, investigate school-age children, plan school locations, and raise funds. Compulsory education committees should be organized at the central, provincial, municipal, and county levels to provide planning.

4. First phase of compulsory education implementation. From the 24th year of the Republic of China to the 28th year, is the period for popularizing one year of compulsory education. At the beginning of this period, each province and city should delineate school districts and widely set up one-year short-term primary schools in each school district, adopting a two-part system, enrolling older out-of-school school-age children aged nine to twelve, so that they receive one year of compulsory education. In addition to being set up independently, these primary schools may also be attached to other primary schools and public institutions. The required school buildings may make full use of public offices, ancestral halls, or rented private houses. If there is nothing to use, extremely simple sheds may be temporarily built. In addition, ordinary primary schools should also be moderately increased, a part of the ordinary primary schools should be required to adopt a two-part system, and the enrollment of existing primary schools should be strengthened. Private schools in various places should be forced to change their curriculum according to the short-term primary school curriculum and be renamed improved private schools. Circuit teaching should be tried out in remote areas, so that at least 80% of the total number of school-age children have received more than one year of compulsory education or ordinary primary school education during these five years.

5. Second phase of implementation. From the 29th year of the Republic of China to the 33rd year, is the period for popularizing two years of compulsory education. The one-year short-term primary schools in each province and city should be gradually changed to three-year short-term primary schools, enrolling out-of-school children aged eight to twelve, so that they receive two years of compulsory education. Other measures implemented in the first phase should continue to be implemented, so that at least 80% of the number of school-age children have received two years of compulsory education or ordinary primary school education.

6. Third phase of implementation. Starting from the 34th year of the Republic of China, in addition to the other measures of the first phase continuing to be implemented, the year-long primary schools in various places should be gradually changed to four-year ordinary primary schools.

7. Fundraising. In addition to the central government's discretionary subsidies, each province and city should also take into account local conditions, either by allocating funds from the provincial and municipal education funds and the provincial and municipal general revenue, or by designating special funds for this purpose. Counties and cities should designate school property or other funds for this purpose according to local conditions.

8. Agencies at all levels. The central government is in charge of the Ministry of Education and organizes the National Compulsory Education Committee to assist in the implementation. The provinces and cities are in charge of the competent educational administrative agencies and organize the provincial, municipal, and county compulsory education committees to assist in the promotion and supervise the use of compulsory education funds.

9. Teacher training. The implementation of compulsory education in various provinces and cities and the promotion of short-term primary schools require many teachers. Short-term primary school teacher training classes should be widely set up in provincial and municipal or county junior middle schools and normal schools, enrolling students with junior middle school graduation qualifications for training. During the first phase, those with clear writing and good reasoning and rich common sense may also be recruited to serve as short-term primary school teachers to meet urgent needs. In addition, each county should set up private school teacher training classes to improve private school teachers. Each province and city should also promote normal schools, simplified normal schools, simplified normal departments, etc., to cultivate primary school teachers.

Hunan Provincial Government Increases Compulsory Education Funds

(Changsha, 15th) The Hunan Provincial Government decided at a regular meeting on the 14th to increase the province's compulsory education funds for the 24th year. It is scheduled to allocate 100,000 yuan in silver in October of the 24th year, 50,000 yuan in January of the 25th year, and 50,000 yuan in May. It also requested a central government subsidy of 150,000 yuan. It also passed the organizational regulations and budget of the Hunan Provincial Public Property Inventory Committee.

Implementation of Compulsory Literacy Education Preliminary Measures in Various Counties of Jiangsu Province

Popular Literacy Education Committees Established in Counties, Districts, Townships, and Groups

(Zhenjiang News) The preliminary measures for compulsory literacy education to be implemented in various counties of Jiangsu Province have been approved by the Provincial Government in its 751st meeting. They are recorded as follows:

Article 1. These measures are specifically formulated for the purpose of implementing compulsory literacy education in Jiangsu Province.

Article 2. Except for counties with special circumstances that have been reported and approved, all counties must conduct compulsory literacy education on a trial basis in accordance with the provisions of these measures. The county magistrate, director of education, and director of public security shall bear absolute responsibility for the promotion of these measures.

Article 3. The county magistrate, director of education, and director of public security in each county must supervise the autonomous regions and districts to organize district popular literacy education committees, and handle compulsory literacy education matters in accordance with the provisions of these measures.

Article 4. The district popular literacy education committee shall be composed of the following personnel, with the district head as chairman: 1. The district head; 2. The head of the social education organization in the district; 3. The head of the public security bureau or the patrolling officer of the branch station in the district; 4. The principal of the complete primary school in the district; 5. The heads of various townships in the district; 6. People in the district who are enthusiastic about education.

Article 5. The functions and powers of the district popular literacy education committee are as follows: 1. Investigate and statistically determine the number of literate and illiterate people in the district; 2. Plan methods for popularizing literacy education in the district; 3. Supervise various townships in carrying out compulsory literacy education; 4. Assess the status of compulsory literacy education in various townships and provide practical guidance; 5. Handle reward and punishment matters related to compulsory literacy education in townships; 6. Other matters.

Article 6. The district popular literacy education committee shall guide various townships to organize township popular literacy education committees to implement popular literacy education matters.

Article 7. The township popular literacy education committee shall be composed of the following personnel, with the township head as chairman: 1. The township head; 2. The principal or head teacher of the primary school within the township; 3. The patrolling officer of the public security branch station or police station within the township; 4. The Bao chiefs of each Bao within the township; 5. People in the township who are enthusiastic about education.

Article 8. The functions and powers of the township popular literacy education committee are as follows: 1. Assist the district popular literacy education committee in handling literacy surveys; 2. Assist the district popular literacy education committee in planning literacy education; 3. Raise funds for the establishment and daily expenses of people's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations; 4. Negotiate and arrange for the location of the aforementioned people's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations; 5. Hire teachers for the aforementioned people's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations, and allocate teaching time; 6. Supervise public and private primary schools and implement the teaching assistant system; 7. Persuade or force illiterate people to enroll; 8. Punish people who should enroll but do not without reason, and report to the district popular literacy education committee for reporting to the county government for record; 9. Other matters.

Article 9. The Bao-Jia chiefs within each township shall be responsible for the following matters related to popular literacy education: 1. Assist in handling investigation and statistical matters; 2. Assist in raising funds; 3. Assist in supervising and forcing enrollment; 4. Other temporary matters.

Article 10. The standards for establishing people's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations in each township are as follows: 1. In towns, each Bao must have at least two people's schools or people's literacy classes; 2. In rural areas, each Bao must have at least one people's school or people's literacy class; 3. If the area of a Bao is too large and it is inconvenient for people to enroll, mobile teaching locations may be set up separately in each Jia; 4. The number of classes and the number of people in each class that should be set up in the previous three items shall be determined based on the number of people who should enroll.

Article 11. The funding methods for people's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations are as follows: 1. The township popular literacy education committee is responsible for raising establishment funds, and may request the county government and education bureau to provide appropriate subsidies; 2. All people's schools established and attached to the counties shall be closed down, and all their funds shall be used to subsidize popular literacy education; 3. The income from public property and other public funds in each township may be submitted to the county government for approval to be allocated to popular literacy education funds; 4. Encourage private donations.

Article 12. People's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations may borrow houses and equipment from the following sources without conditions: 1. Primary schools and social education institutions; 2. Temples and ancestral halls; 3. Private schools; 4. Public meeting places; 5. Others. The above-mentioned locations must unconditionally accept the borrowing of houses and equipment for people's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations, and must not refuse for any reason.

Article 13. The teachers of people's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations are all volunteer positions, and shall be appointed by the township popular literacy education committee from the following personnel: 1. Current primary school principals or teachers; 2. Teachers of social education institutions; 3. Current private school teachers; 4. Various public officials within the county; 5. Graduates of senior primary schools or above who currently reside in the district; 6. Schools may adopt the teaching assistant system for fourth-grade students; 7. Other people who are enthusiastic about education. The above-mentioned personnel must unconditionally accept the appointment as teachers when people's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations are invited, and must not refuse for any reason, but may pay for someone to act as an agent. The teaching time shall be shared equally by those with teaching qualifications in the township.

Article 14. After the establishment of people's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations, enrollment shall be encouraged or forced immediately. The main points are as follows: 1. After the opening and establishment of people's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations, the Bao-Jia chiefs shall separately encourage those who should enroll to do so; 2. If no one in a household over the age of sixteen is literate, at least one person must be taught in a people's school, people's literacy class, or mobile teaching location; 3. If enrollment is not achieved after more than three encouragements, imprisonment or fines shall be imposed until enrollment is achieved. Measures for imprisonment or fines will be formulated separately.

Article 15. The people's schools, people's literacy classes, and mobile teaching locations organized in accordance with these measures must pay attention to the following points: 1. The teaching subject should be literacy as the main subject; 2. The teaching materials must adopt textbooks approved by the Ministry of Education, and may compile supplementary teaching materials; 3. The teaching time shall be based on the time that does not hinder the people's working hours; 4. The study period shall be four months, but may be shortened or extended as appropriate.

Article 16. The county magistrate of each county must, together with the director of education and the director of public security, formulate a detailed implementation plan, procedure, and completion period in accordance with the provisions of these measures, and submit it to the Department of Education for approval and implementation.

Article 17. The county magistrate, director of education, director of public security, district head, township head, Jia chief, head of social education institution, and school principal of each county shall be rewarded or punished separately after assessment for their achievements or lack of progress in popular literacy education. The assessment and reward and punishment measures will be formulated separately.

Article 18. After these measures are completed, a second step will be formulated and implemented.

Article 19. These measures shall be passed and implemented by the members of the Jiangsu Provincial Government, and shall be forwarded to the Ministry of Education for record.

China Children's Culture Association Held Inaugural Meeting Yesterday

Discussed Articles of Association and Issued Declaration of Establishment

The China Children's Culture Association held its inaugural meeting at the Shenbao Supplementary School in the mainland shopping mall at 2:00 PM yesterday, discussed the articles of association, passed proposals, elected officers, and issued a declaration of establishment. The details are recorded as follows:

Attending Members

Hu Shuyi, Chen Jicheng, Zhou Shang, Wei Bingxin, Huang Jiping, Lin Yin, Sun Yucai, Huang Jingwan, Yuan Dingchang, Zhao Yun, Lv Boyou, Ni Xiying, Bai Tao, Shao Mingjiu, Yu Songhua, Qian Zaozai, Huang Chuncai, Yan Zhenyu, and more than 100 other members attended. Wang Longzhang, a representative from the municipal party headquarters, attended to provide guidance.

Meeting Proceedings

The meeting started at 2:00 PM. The presidium included Chen Jicheng, Hu Shuyi, Huang Jiping, Shao Mingjiu, etc. Bai Tao was the secretary, and Sun Yucai and Huang Jingwan were the general managers. After the formalities were completed, the chairman delivered the opening remarks, and Lin Yin reported on the preparations. Next, Wang Longzhang, a representative from the municipal party headquarters, delivered a speech. Hu Shuyi, Zhou Shang, and others gave speeches. Then, the articles of association were discussed and proposals were passed. Finally, officers were elected and the meeting adjourned after a group photo.

Proposals Passed

(1) Publish a regular journal; (2) Formulate branch articles of association and organize branches for members in various places; (3) Hold regular children's book and newspaper exhibitions; (4) Set up a children's book and newspaper vehicle; (5) Send representatives to participate in the preparation for the opening ceremony of Shanghai Children's Year; (6) Hold regular seminars, visits, picnics, and dinners; (7) Set up children's news agencies in various places and compile and print communication magazines; (8) Organize children's circulating libraries; (9) Edit popular books and organize an editorial review committee; (10) Request government subsidies; (11) Establish a fixed location for the association.

Elected Officers

The elected directors are Huang Jiping, Chen Jicheng, Lin Yin, Bai Tao, Sun Yucai, He Gongchao, Huang Chuncai, Wei Bingxin, Hu Shuyi, Zhou Shang, Wang Longzhang, Yuan Dingchang, Ni Xiying, Huang Jingwan, Qian Xuanqing, Xu Yingchang, Chen Peide, Li Chucai, and Song Yi, totaling 19 people. The elected supervisors are Yan Zhenyu, Ma Chonggan, Zhao Yun, Yu Songhua, and Fan Yuntian, totaling 5 people.

Declaration of Establishment

Draft of the China Children's Culture Association Declaration: In our country, children have always been forgotten. They are appendages of adults, playthings of adults. They have no freedom, no education. What adults give them is one: beating, two: deception, three: teaching them to completely submit and be slaves. The rich sons and daughters enjoy happiness at home, as playthings. Some study books in a pile of books. The poor raise cattle and work for others, wander the streets, and are little beggars. Otherwise, they are sold or abandoned by their parents. What adults give children is a cruel world, a world of slaves, a world of deception, a world of terror. However, the government has now officially announced that Children's Year will begin on August 1st of this year, and has formulated measures to protect children. From now on, this world belongs to children. We want to break the world created by adults and liberate children, especially liberating their hands and brains, to create a new children's world. In the children's world, there is only justice and no cruelty, only freedom and no oppression, only creation and no inheritance, only people among people and no people above people. It is a world of freedom, equality, mutual assistance, and self-defense. This world does not belong to a few children, but to the masses of children. We must not only care for this part and forget that part. We who are purely serving children's culture should unite and strive for this new culture. We are not building well for children to enjoy happiness, but transforming into a part of the children's world to participate in this work. We are a living cell in the children's world, helping the children's world grow. The work we need to do now is to promote all children's cultural construction, study all children's problems, study children's education, create children's science, children's literature, children's art, improve children's health, improve children's entertainment, and so on. At present, on the one hand, we will re-evaluate all the old children's culture, and on the other hand, create the most rationalized children's culture in the children's world. This is our declaration.

Economic Supplement

The Financial Industry's Subsequent Awakening

— Wang Jingshi

The financial industry essentially exists to regulate the financial turnover deficiencies in various industrial and commercial sectors, indirectly assisting in the prosperity of various industries, thereby achieving a collective path towards overall economic prosperity. Therefore, as industry and commerce become more developed, the need for financial turnover increases, and the financial business becomes more prosperous. Thus, the financial industry becomes more prosperous due to the prosperity of industry and commerce, and more consolidated due to the development of industry and commerce. Conversely, industry and commerce, through the various assistance of the financial industry and the convenience of capital flow, can further develop various industries, and even the entire social economy benefits directly and indirectly. From this, the great contribution of the financial industry to the development prospects of industry and commerce is evident; at the same time, the concern of industry and commerce for the prosperity of the financial industry is also evident. The two are mutually beneficial and indispensable. If industry and commerce lack the financial support of the financial industry, progress is difficult. It is also a practical impossibility for the financial industry to detach itself from industry and commerce and exist and prosper independently. Therefore, the two can prosper together only by coexisting. During periods of economic panic, the two should cooperate closely to plan properly in order to break the deadlock. Otherwise, both sides will inevitably suffer heavy losses, which can be asserted. However, in recent years, industry and commerce have been affected internally by rural bankruptcy and externally by the global economic recession, the situation has taken a sharp turn for the worse, and is declining daily. The financial industry is also feeling difficult to cope with due to the sluggishness of domestic industrial and commercial sectors, and at the same time threatened by the US silver policy. As a result, the financial industry, which previously specialized in rescuing and regulating the capital of various industries, had to make great efforts to tighten up, resulting in a situation where it was not only unable to save others, but even unable to save itself. The closure and bankruptcy of money shops and banks in various places last year fully demonstrates the deepening of the economic panic, and the financial crisis is following industry and commerce. This seriousness deserves our attention. Now, let's list the financial institutions that have suspended operations in various places:

Location Number of Bankruptcies Total Capital Reasons for Bankruptcy

Jiujiang 5 120,000 Poor management, grain business failure

Shantou 3 Not specified Insufficient turnover, business failure

Wuxi 4 270,000 Affected by low prices of silk and rice

Ningbo 9 369,000 Insufficient turnover, shareholders unwilling to operate

Wuhu 2 70,000 Loans unrecoverable

Baoding 3 130,000 Business failure, shareholder discord

Changchun 4 60,000 Voluntary closure and losses

Qintong 3 120,000 Doubtful accounts

Shijiazhuang 5 28,000 Depressed market, insufficient turnover

Quzhou 3 72,000 Business downturn, voluntary liquidation

Anqing 2 70,000 Doubtful accounts, insufficient turnover

Andong 5 85,000 Shareholder discord, unwilling to operate

Chengdu 1 150,000 Losses from Chongqing remittances, interest losses

Hangzhou 2 60,000 Capital loss, unwilling to operate

Jiaxing 5 126,000 Business decline, shareholders unwilling to operate

Tunxi 1 10,000 Business downturn, speculative failure

Yuyao 2 40,000 Difficult turnover

Dalian 2 82,500 Business downturn, shareholder discord

Neijiang 2 20,000 Excessive losses by manager

Zhenjiang 1 Not specified Insufficient turnover

Tianjin 3 (Silver shops) Not specified Business downturn, shareholder discord

Wenzhou 3 33,000 Too many bad debts, insufficient turnover

Hong Kong 5 1,600,000 Poor business, real estate losses

Yantai 3 68,000 Too many bad debts, unable to maintain

Shenyang 1 300,000 Too many loans, unable to recover

Taiyuan 1 50,000 Not specified

Dinghai 2 30,000 Shareholder debts, empty assets

Jinhua 3 61,600 Difficult to recover loans, insufficient turnover

Shanghai 8 2,038,000 Bad debts and real estate losses, weak assets

Pinghu 2 Not specified Market decline, years of losses

The above list only concerns money shops, and already 113 have ceased operations, with a total capital of about 10 million yuan. Looking at the banks that have failed in various places, such as the China Savings Bank, Wuhua Bank, China Industrial Bank, Jiande Bank, Wing On Silver Company, Oriental Trust Company, Overseas Chinese Trust Company, Huadong Bank, Jia Hua Bank, Tong Yi Bank, Xiamen Commercial Savings Bank, Anhui Bank, Jiaxing Commercial Savings Bank, and recently the Minghua Commercial Savings Bank and the foreign-owned American Feng Bank, etc. Since 1930, more than 30 have suspended operations, with a capital of more than 30 million yuan! In addition to the exceptions mentioned above, omissions are inevitable. If there were accurate surveys and statistics, it would undoubtedly be even more impressive. If we analyze the reasons for the closures, they are nothing more than weak capital, insufficient turnover, speculative failures, real estate mortgage losses, too many bad debts, and withdrawals, etc. Industry and commerce are inevitably in a state of collapse due to the termination of assistance. Therefore, in recent years, news of industrial and commercial bankruptcies has been constantly coming, and it is truly chilling! However, in this critical situation, we cannot but raise the following questions. That is, will the financial industry listen to the natural trends, seeking only current survival, and even not hesitate to separate from industry and commerce! Will industry and commerce also drastically tighten up and not seek to struggle? If this is the case, both sides will suffer heavy losses, which is undeniable. To break this deadlock, the financial industry must shoulder this heavy responsibility, and the financial industry must pay attention to the following points.

First, from the perspective of money shops, the reasons for their bankruptcy can be summarized as follows:

1. Weak capital: The capital of most money shops is mostly between 20,000 to 30,000 yuan, and up to 100,000 yuan. May I ask, can tens of thousands of yuan of funds meet the needs of society? Even if it can be dealt with, it must be turned over quickly to avoid worries. A slight stagnation will reveal flaws. If tens of thousands of yuan of funds are concentrated on a few targets, once there is a risk, there is also the risk of being affected and going bankrupt. Therefore, money shops in the future should cooperate, concentrate capital, and increase their strength. This is one point.

2. Stagnant accounts: When money shops lend money, they often focus on people as the object, and ignore material credit. This point is psychologically welcomed by society. However, in the modern society, there are many complex careers, which are by no means as simple as in the past. Moreover, in the midst of economic turmoil, there are dangers lurking everywhere. If the object of the loan encounters an unfortunate event, and the loan has no corresponding collateral to compensate, then the money shop itself will immediately be shaken. This point should be urgently noted in terms of loan granting to avoid danger. This is the second point.

3. Poor organization: The organization of money shops is mostly limited to the old style. For example, if investors agree with each other for a moment, they will contribute funds to form a group. Once the benefits are not evenly distributed, they will often hinder each other. Not only will the business be affected, but the business itself will also face a crisis. Moreover, the purpose of the organization is mostly only to obtain profits, and does not consider how to expand and how to serve the society. Therefore, money shops that have been around for decades "remain the same." From this, it can be seen that the money industry has shallow vision and weak initiative. Imperfect organization further hinders business operations. This is the third point that should be noted.

The above three points are for money shops. Next, the following points should also be realized by banks:

1. Excessive concentration of business: According to the 1933 Bank Yearbook, there are 146 head offices and 891 branch offices of banks nationwide, totaling 1,038. Among them, the nine cities of Shanghai, Tianjin, Beiping, Qingdao, Hangzhou, Suzhou, Nanjing, Chongqing, Hankou, and Guangzhou have a total of 95 head offices, accounting for 65% of the total, and 311 branch offices, accounting for 30% of the total. The provinces of Jiangsu and Zhejiang have the most, with a total of 24 head offices, accounting for 16% of the total, and 182 branch offices, accounting for 18% of the total. From this, it can be seen that the development of banks in my country is clearly biased towards urban and coastal provinces. Since the banking business is concentrated in the same area, the investment path must become narrow. Those with weak capital are often overwhelmed by those with strong capital, and they have no choice but to tend towards speculation in order to obtain profits. This creates an excess of banks and increases panic. This is one point.

2. Excessive uniformity of investment: The current investment paths of banks tend to be uniform. For example, if Bank A thinks that a certain industry is profitable, Bank B will also imitate it. As a result, loans are excessively granted, and once there is a risk, everyone suffers. Or, for emerging industries with promising prospects, which urgently need funds, they hesitate to move forward. The inability of industry and commerce in our country to prosper due to this kind of environment is very common. Moreover, even if the amount of the loan is not large, they refuse to consider it, and do not ask about the future of the industry, and do not accept it at all. They would rather invest the capital that could be used for production in places of extravagance. This is truly puzzling, and it is not the attitude that the financial industry should have in serving, nor is it the original intention of the financial industry to support social industries. Small-capital industrial and commercial enterprises may not have weaker credit than large enterprises, and the future of small-capital industrial and commercial enterprises may not be able to achieve development one day. Moreover, the amount is smaller, and it is more convenient to take out and redeem loans, the risk is lighter, and the degree of profit accumulation is no less than that of large loans. The financial industry should pay close attention to this. This is the second point.

3. Small-capital banks should merge: Most of the reasons for the bankruptcy of various banks are due to weak capital, which leads to temporary insufficient turnover. Therefore, it can be seen that it is not easy for small banks to stand. Because the capital is not large, it is difficult to gain the trust of customers psychologically, and in terms of absorbing deposits, they have to use high interest rates as a slogan, hoping to compete with larger banks. At the same time, in terms of the way out for funds, they naturally have to obtain better profits. In this time of economic depression, productive industries are of course unable to bear the exploitation, so they have to turn to speculation, or proceed regardless of the size of the risk, only seeking generous interest. Once they fail, they cannot but be sacrificed as a result. The intangible is nothing more than increasing the degree of panic. Therefore, I deeply feel that, under the current circumstances, are we only seeking to increase the number of banks to decorate the market? Or are we seeking to enrich the quality to maintain industry and commerce? The greatest need at present is naturally the latter. Therefore, I earnestly hope that the financial industry itself will gather most of the small capital and become several strong and powerful capital. In terms of business, it can naturally avoid the danger of being squeezed, and at the same time, it is easy to gain social trust. In the future, the factors of panic can also be reduced a lot. This is the third point.

In addition to the above points, there is also a common problem in the financial industry, which is the excessively high interest rates. This not only puts great constraints on industry and commerce, preventing them from developing as much as possible; the financial industry itself is also subject to many obstacles. Therefore, in the future, under the conditions of mutual cooperation, interest rates should be reduced urgently. If the interest rate is reduced on the deposit side, the interest rate on loans can also be reduced. As a result, industry and commerce can also avoid a lot of harsh burdens; and gradually have the opportunity to recover and revive. The revival of industry and commerce in the financial industry is indirectly the expansion of the way out for legitimate investment! Undoubtedly, under this condition of mutual cooperation, the degree of economic panic can easily be transformed from deepening to prosperity!

Preventing Drought

— Wu Xiaochen

China, plagued by frequent natural disasters and man-made calamities, after each devastating and painful catastrophe, the entire country invariably trembles with the fear of the recurrence of misfortune, but as time passes and the situation changes, it is forgotten in the blink of an eye, and no one has ever seen preventive measures taken to prevent harm from occurring and eliminate harm invisibly. Take waterlogging and drought as examples. They occur almost every year, which is evident. The severity of the drought and famine last summer opened up a severe phenomenon unseen in sixty years. The affected provinces included as many as eleven provinces, including Jiangsu, Zhejiang, Anhui, Jiangxi, Hunan, Hubei, Henan, Hebei, Gansu, Guizhou, and Shanxi, totaling 635 counties. The affected area was 329 million mu, accounting for 47% of the cultivated land area of the eleven provinces. According to post-event estimates, the losses in terms of quantity were: 216 million dan of rice, 31.2 million dan of sorghum, 25 million dan of corn, 40 million dan of millet, 6 million dan of cotton, and 31.6 million dan of soybeans; in terms of value: rice was worth 684 million yuan, sorghum was worth 72 million yuan, corn was worth 67 million yuan, soybeans were worth 129 million yuan, cotton was worth 199 million yuan, and millet was worth 917 million yuan, totaling more than 1.7 billion yuan! In the counties affected by the disaster last autumn, there was even no harvest, with wailing and misery everywhere, and starving people on the road. Today, recalling these thrilling figures, can we not, in addition to being sincerely terrified, realize that the past cannot be remedied and that the future can be pursued?

The water conservancy and rivers of Jiangsu and Zhejiang provinces are crisscrossed, and they have always been known for their superiority over other provinces. Moreover, each county also levies water conservancy expenses under the land tax. There should be no worries about funds for water conservancy construction. However, when the drought comes, they can only sit back and watch without any measures and cannot be exempt from disasters. We fully expect that the silk industry will improve this spring, and we will make up for the losses in mulberry trees. How can we know that the decline in cocoon prices is even more severe than in the past, and the heavy burden of donations and taxes has increased rather than decreased. The suffering and displacement are unspeakable. At this time, it is the rainy season, and farmers are just starting to cultivate the land and eagerly waiting for rain. However, Henan, Shandong, Hebei and other provinces have already reported drought. The soil in Lingbao and other places is dry and cracked, and it is said that flower seeds cannot be sown. Recently, early signs have also been seen in southern Anhui, with seedlings withering, and the Xu and Hai prefectures have not had penetrating rain for two months. Even the fields are dry and cracked, and farmers in the four townships are praying for rain. In Beijing, Changzhou and other places, the farmland is also dry, and a drought is about to occur. The scene of farmland in Zhejiang is that the seedlings are several inches long, but there is no water to transplant. For days, the south wind has been blowing, the sky is clear and the weather is bright, and there is no sign of the rainy season at all. I don't know when the rain will come. If we don't take urgent preventive measures, there will still be a drought this year, and the people will have no food to eat. At the time of the severe drought last year, we also thought about water conservancy and raised a large amount of debt, hoping to use it for disaster relief and work-for-relief in the disaster areas. But what is the fact? Perhaps the disaster area is so large that our people cannot know it. We believe that today's disaster prevention should focus on three points: Salvaging what can be saved, first, widespread placement of water lifting equipment, second, dredging of rivers, and third, planting drought-resistant crops. Let's discuss them separately:

The original water lifting equipment in rural areas, whether relying on wind power or livestock power, has very little water lifting capacity. During the severe drought last year, the weather was scorching above, and the river water became shallower day by day below. The length of the water wheel was limited, and irrigation was not easy. The water demand of the fields doubled, and the supply was even more difficult. Although the farmers worked day and night, and used manpower to supplement the shortcomings of livestock and wind power, the crops still could not avoid withering. This is like a cup of water on a cartload of firewood, which cannot be helped by the original water lifting equipment. However, rural families have experienced several ups and downs in recent years and are living below the poverty line. It is impossible for them to afford to purchase practical water pumps. Although the various sectors helped to purchase them last year to relieve the urgent need, there were too few porridge and too many monks, and they failed to achieve universal results. However, the advantages of water pumps for serious matters are incomparable to the original water lifting equipment, which is known to everyone. The way to prevent drought is to widely install water pumps as the initial step in preventing drought. It would be even better if electricity could be used for irrigation. The government should order the provinces and instruct the cities and counties to make overall plans and provide financial assistance from the government.

I still remember that when the drought was raging last summer, the river water was completely dry in the higher terrain, and even drinking water was a panic. The residents upstream of the river competed to block it, so that those downstream could not get a drop of water. Therefore, the dredging of the river. Not only should the above-mentioned canal projects be completed as soon as possible, but other tributaries and small streams should also be considered, otherwise, even if there are water pumps, it will be in vain.

Due to the different psychological states of farmers in various places, the crops are not uniform, one province is like this, one county is like this, and even one town and one village are like this. Chinese farmers rely on the sky for food, and all the waxing and waning are tied to the sky, and they follow the evolution of nature and cannot use manpower to adapt to changes; and under the consistent thinking of farmers, there are few opportunities to improve farming. Therefore, as last year when Jiaxing farmland was shrouded in drought, there were completely different results: the Wangdian area of Jiana is all rice fields, which need a lot of water. After the drought and famine, there was no way to supply water, resulting in withered rice and cracked soil, and no harvest. However, the ginger fields in the Xinfeng area of Jiabei had surprisingly good harvests, because ginger fields need very little water and are afraid of hot summer days. Sudden thunderstorms can cause the ginger stems to develop fever. During the severe drought last summer, there was no thunder or rain. This weather is most suitable for the growth of ginger, so last year's ginger fields had a good harvest due to the good process, which is the opposite of the rice fields in the Wangdian area. There are also rice fields in the Haiyan County, and 19 out of 10 were withered and died. Only the cotton fields in Huangwan did not lose their original vitality due to the drought, which is the opposite of the rice fields. In normal years, there is no worry about water shortage, only fear of too much water, so it is not affected by the severe drought at all. Originally, if the two counties of Haiyan and Haiyan were relatively high in western Zhejiang, it was more difficult than any other county to divert water for irrigation in the years of waterlogging and drought, so it is necessary to study whether the farmland in the two counties is suitable for permanent rice cultivation. In China, where natural disasters occur every year, there is no active way to prevent disasters from happening for a while, so we have to plant more drought-resistant crops, hoping to reduce the degree of disasters.

The Soviet Union's Grain Control Process

— Huang Yingdai

Turning to the economic history of the Soviet Union in 1935, one of the most important pages is the abolition of grain rationing. In the past year, there have been significant changes to the wage standards in various industries in the Soviet Union. On March 17 of that year, the government explicitly ordered the correction of labor laws and the abolition of restrictions on the minimum wage system throughout the Soviet Union; in recent years, the Soviet industrial sector had established a low-wage system, and many factories had guarantees regarding the so-called low wage. However, this new decree only abolished the restrictions on the low wages earned by general workers. Only if various industries fall into a state of stagnation through no fault of the workers, the workers should receive one-third of their usual wages. Since June 1 of last year, the wage system has been changed again in the opposite direction, in order to reconcile the impact of the rising bread prices in the ration, it was explicitly ordered to increase wages in various industries by 10 to 15 percent. According to the news released by the government, the most beneficial thing after the promulgation of this new decree is that 4.2 million workers with the lowest wages, their current average monthly wage is 92 rubles, (this type of worker includes 140,000 low-level miners) and the monthly expenditure is only 79 rubles. A few weeks later, a supplementary law was promulgated, giving employees whose "work has considerable military relationship" an additional 10 percent increase in wages. However, the benefits given to workers by this change in the wage system have unfortunately become castles in the air, as the government simultaneously reduced the value of rubles for workers to purchase goods. Not only did they raise the price of bread, but they also changed the supply system. Since the Soviet Union re-adopted the grain rationing coupon system five years ago, the value of the ruble has had no fixed standard, it depends on the source of all owners and supplies at any time. Those with privileges can represent a value of three pounds and five ounces of bread or six ounces of cream with one ruble. However, those who are treated more poorly can only exchange their ruble for 11 and three-quarters ounces of bread, or the same one ounce of cream. Factory workers can get the cheapest food, of which bread can be exchanged daily at the lowest price, bread coupons can be distributed regularly, meat, cream, wheat flour, and other less produced items are rarely distributed, and they can also be distributed from the beginning of last year, but there is no fixed time and the limit is insufficient.

The so-called grain rationing was created in the Soviet Union in 1917. However, it was abolished by the Soviet Union government ten years ago. During the implementation of the New Economic Policy (1921-1928), private enterprises and profitable matters were allowed, food and other commodities could be sold publicly in stores and markets with very few restrictions, even rare goods and goods pricing were not restricted. In 1929, the Soviet Union re-adopted a chaotic system of item rationing, including food, clothing, and other various items, as part of the five-year economic plan. As for various stores, which are commonly seen in other countries, were completely abolished in the Soviet Union for about three years. If the people of the Soviet Union did not get the permission of the authorities, even the acquisition of a pair of shoes or a piece of soap was considered illegal. This distribution system has now been completely abolished. Recently, at the Communist Party Congress, Domestic Supply People's Commissar Mikoyan reported on the failure of this system, therefore, the Communist Party had long decided in its ideals to restore the open sale of goods in stores, adopt a new system of "state-run stores," and sell goods directly to customers. In fact, the item rationing system has long been abolished, and other commodities, except for food, can currently be purchased in various stores, and the quantity is not restricted. However, the prices of all commodities in these stores are regulated by the government, which is unfortunate for the general customers. The prices set are too high for the Soviet low-level workers. In this type of open store, butter is roughly eight rubles per pound, meat is two and two-tenths rubles per pound, sugar is four and a half rubles per pound, tea is eight rubles per pound, and eggs are half a ruble per basket. Therefore, the commodities that workers can exchange for their monthly wage of 92 rubles are limited. Even calculating the prices in gold pounds is of no help. The exchange rates stipulated by the Moscow government are only intended for foreign tourists who need to exchange at the price, and there is no other intention. As for special stores that supply the needs of customers who carry foreign currency, the exchange rates set by the government are not valued by the Soviet authorities either.

In the past few years, factory workers could buy regularly distributed bread and other irregularly distributed foods at the lowest price every day, so although their wages were low, they could still maintain their lives. However, since the change in the status of workers in June of the previous year, their lives have become more difficult, and the increase in wages is enough to make them lose their eligibility to receive the lowest-priced food. Workers still need two and one-fifth pounds of bread and some other food every day. However, the 92 rubles they earn today are worth less than the 83 rubles they earned last year. They can buy all kinds of goods in the open market, but the prices are much more expensive than in state-run stores. In addition, there are foreign national food supply stores that are exclusively for foreign nationals to buy goods, and there are many goods, but they only supply foreign currency or precious metals, and do not supply Soviet workers to buy goods. How low the price of agricultural products obtained by farmers is and how high the price paid by urban residents is, the government has never explained. The method of obtaining agricultural products and transporting them to cities is entirely in the hands of the state, and urban residents only trade directly in the spring and winter seasons of the year. After farmers have completed their grain delivery obligations to the government, a few months are stipulated as a period of permission, and barter is completely prohibited. Those who act as intermediaries in a private capacity have been openly reduced. Because intermediaries can obtain a lot of profit by introducing farmers' products for factory consumption, and their position has now been completely replaced by the government. The interest rate charged by this new intermediary is something that outsiders cannot know, except that merchants from various countries can dream of it. We can prove that the supply of food in the Soviet Union is completely monopolized by the government.

In general, farmers must pay the prescribed grains for every hundred acres of land suitable for cultivation as a compulsory tax. The remaining grains are encouraged by government agencies and state-owned cooperative agencies to sell them at agreed prices according to special decrees. The grains obtained by the above two methods are used to supply the army, factories, shops, and for export. The grains obtained by farmers for paying compulsory taxes are valued at 72 rubles per ton for buckwheat and 88 rubles for wheat. The same grains are valued at 90 rubles per ton for buckwheat and 100 rubles for wheat when farmers sell them to the state voluntarily. The government wholesales this buckwheat to various factories at a price of 525 rubles per ton and 600 rubles for wheat. These grains are then ground into flour by the factories to make low-priced bread. Therefore, the government makes a profit of six times more on the grains sold to factories under the grain rationing system. The bread sold by state-run stores, made from buckwheat, costs one and three-quarters rubles per pound, and the bread made from wheat costs two rubles per pound, making even more profit. Therefore, customers have to pay 30 to 40 times more for bread sold openly in state-run stores than for the bread directly distributed to farmers by the government. The government has a monopoly on the supply of bread needed by urban residents, which is obvious. The amount of grain collected is not very appropriate for supplying the needs of the army and cities. As for whether farmers agree with this system, there is no clear indication, and the authorities are not interested in considering this issue. The government has declared that the grain rationing system will be abolished and is preparing to supply all the needs of the people with new stores. If the government intends to equalize the prices of food in stores with the wages of industries, it will be easy. The government is currently sacrificing a large part of the tax rate levied on urban residents, but the benefits obtained are still inappropriate. Those who operate similar stores in various countries must know the reason. The so-called sacrifice, such as raising wages or lowering prices, or both, is the main issue before the government abolishes the central item rationing system and re-establishes open stores, because if the people are completely separated from the item rationing system and wages and prices are not corrected in advance, it is tantamount to pushing low-wage laborers into starvation.

Grain: Rainy Weather Allows the Rice Market to See a Settlement

Asphalt is in the era of falling orders. Candle washing has stopped. Most soap making has switched to using coconut oil, butter, etc., so that the asphalt sales market is almost unattended.
